Ju Zheng's Report at the National Government Memorial Week 46

Stabilizing the Turmoil of the Political Situation

And Completing the Communist Suppression Work

(Nanjing) The National Government held its memorial week on the morning of the 25th. Ju Zheng, Yu Youren, Chen Shaokuan, Li Yuanding, Lin Xiang, Lu Qu, Wei Huai, and more than 400 National Government officials attended. Chairman Lin led the ceremony. Ju Zheng gave a report entitled Stabilizing the Turmoil of the Political Situation and Actively Completing the Bandit Suppression Work. The original words are as follows: Today, brothers want to report on two points. One is to stabilize the turmoil of the political situation, and the other is to actively complete the bandit suppression work. Regarding the first point, the central government has always used the four words "sincerity and unity" to hope that all comrades in the party who bear important military and political responsibilities will give up their prejudices and support the central government in overcoming the current difficulties together. Therefore, on the one hand, it is striving for the stability of the political situation, opening up a way out, and giving the country an opportunity to gradually implement all construction plans. Because the Chinese political situation is often in turmoil, just like the ripples caused by throwing a stone into a pool of clear water, there is a limit. If stones are constantly thrown down, the pool water will be in a long-term state of turmoil. The current Chinese political situation is like the pool water that has been thrown stones into. There are many people throwing stones, and the turmoil of the political situation is even worse. Therefore, the greatest obstacle to China's political reform is in this state of throwing stones. It is even more obstructed. We can imagine that any ideal of political reform must take unity and stability as its premise for implementation. Otherwise, all the nice-sounding political terms will be empty talk. In recent years, the government's painstaking efforts to seek unity and stability have been based on this principle. However, the facts obtained are very contrary. If it is said that Chinese politics is truly in a state of unity and stability, then even if there are many different doctrines and political parties opposed to each other, such as the current situation in Britain and the United States, it can also constrain and summarize all political struggles within the scope of the law, and build a country that is more perfect than China is at present. This is very obvious. But does China's current situation have these conditions? Can all the doctrines of Europe and the United States be moved out for political struggle? If not, then we must first create a situation of unity and stability for political transformation. This is the consistent position of the central government. But how can we achieve unity and security? This depends on whether the comrades in the party who are responsible for the military and political affairs can attach importance to the party's doctrine and believe that the wrong idea of harming the nation by throwing stones is wrong. Otherwise, the future turmoil of the Chinese political situation will only have a hopeless future and will inevitably cause the entire nation to perish together. Therefore, at this time, the central government can only seek perfection and hope that the comrades in the party will be tolerant and support the central government so that the turmoil can move toward stability. Regarding the second point, actively completing the bandit suppression work is the fact that the government has been working with all its strength in recent years. The scourge of the Communist bandits in China lies not in their own rampant power, but in the fact that our government and comrades are not properly suppressed. We must actively use the political line and goals of the Three People's Principles to eliminate that group of bandits who have long been ignorant of what politics is. The past work of suppressing the Communists has achieved good results, and the generals who suppressed the Communists have long put forward the proposition of 30% military and 70% politics. This is truly saying that the struggle between nationalism and anti-nationalism is, in other words, not only a military struggle, but also a political struggle. Therefore, to complete the fundamental task of suppressing the bandits, the struggle in military and politics must be attached to a supreme rule at the same time. At the same time, as an aspect of the political struggle, such as the bloody battles of the armed forces in the front, it should be carried out with the slogan of 30% military and 70% politics. Then, the cultural contention in the rear should also be carried out with the slogan of 30% thought and 70% politics. The reason is that communism is spreading in China, and only by eradicating this ideological poison can we eradicate it. But we can also know that the communist scourge in China is manifested in ideology on the one hand, and in action on the other hand. Only the struggle of action can eradicate this poison of action. We must assume the responsibility of suppressing the bandits with this point of view, so that the military and political work will not fail. Only in this way can we have the hope of unity and stability. The armed comrades in the front and the long-shirt comrades in the rear, the national crisis is imminent, and everyone should work hard to complete this work to save the last fate of this country and nation. (Central News Agency Telegraph, 25th)

Liang Hejun Discusses the Administrative Situation in Ningxia 57

Requests the Central Government to Provide Favorable Resettlement for Sun Dianying's Troops

(Nanjing) Liang Hejun, Director of the Finance Department of Ningxia Province, arrived in Beijing on the 25th from Ningxia at the invitation of Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi. He visited President Wang Jingwei and reported on the recent administrative situation in the province. He said that since Ningxia became a province, the administrative situation has improved. The stationed troops in the province do not interfere in politics, which is rare in other provinces. On the revenue side, there has been a gradual increase. The annual tax revenue of the entire province is about 3.5 million yuan, with fur accounting for more than 60-70%. Payment of military and government expenses is still slightly surplus. Ma Hongkui's 15th Route Army receives an additional 80,000 yuan per month from the Central Government, so it feels more stable. Although agricultural crops have been abundant in recent years, prices are too low, so the entire province's rural areas are showing signs of bankruptcy. Sun Dianying's troops from the Central Government entered Qinghai to reclaim land. After arriving in the area from Qinghai to Suiyuan, the people of Qinghai could not bear the burden and protested, requesting the Central Government to withdraw the order. The discipline of Sun's troops is still good. Currently, Suiyuan is below zero degrees Celsius, and Sun's army does not take a single blade of grass or tree from the people. This time I came to Beijing, in addition to reporting to the Central Government, I also ask the Central Government to pay attention to Sun's troops and give them favorable resettlement. (25th Special Dispatch)

The 19th Route Army Has Not Yet Advanced to Jianou 99

The Focus of Communist Suppression in the North Road Shifts to Northern Fujian 100

——Chiang Kai-shek Orders Various Units to Pursue and Suppress the Communists in Fujian——

A Nanchang dispatch reports that since the Fujian Incident, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has been actively suppressing the pseudo 1357 Army Corps gathered on the border between Jiangxi and Fujian, without any relaxation, in order to break the cooperation between the bandits and the Fujian side. The bandits in Zixi and Lichuan have already been defeated and retreated into Fujian. The focus of the bandit suppression has shifted from eastern Jiangxi to northern Fujian. Recently, Chiang Kai-shek personally went to the front line to command and supervise the troops to closely pursue the bandits in northern Fujian. Various units captured Guangze on the 11th. Except for a small part of the pseudo 7th Army Corps retreating to Guangchang, a large part of it fled into the area of Tai Ning and Shunchang in Fujian. After the North Road Army recovered Guangze, the Guande Pass was under control. In Jiangxi, the intrusion of the Red Army can be prevented, and in Fujian, it can stand together with the Central Army of Chong'an and Shaowu, and cooperate with various units on the Zhejiang border. If the Fujian army invades Zhejiang, the Central Army can cut off its rear. Moreover, the terrain of Fujian is high in the west and low in the east, and the Central Army can attack the back of the Fujian army. Therefore, the Fuzhou Camp has been moved to to facilitate command. (December 20)

Guangdong Army Patrols Entire Fujian Border 101

19th Route Army Air Force Mobilizes Northward

A Significant Number of Red Bandits Secretly Arrive in Changting and Liancheng

Shantou Correspondence: Following the Fujian Incident, the Guangdong side actively consolidated its border defenses. Currently, the forwardmost patrols of the Guangdong army along the Guangdong-Fujian border have crossed into Fujian. They can reach Zhangzhou and Longyan within 24 hours. The entire 19th Route Army is moving towards Fuzhou and northern Fujian. In the Xingquan area, there are only some newly formed militia units under Weng Zhaoyuan. Zhangzhou also only has the 49th Division under Zhang Yan, at most no more than three regiments. The Guangdong army patrols along the Zhao'an road every night, with patrols only a little over ten li from the county seat. It is said that He Shijun, the Magistrate of Zhao'an County, went to Macau for medical treatment last month. The Fujian Provincial Government then appointed Yang Shaokai as the new Magistrate, but Yang has not yet taken office. With no one in charge of county affairs, the county soldiers and militia suddenly mutinied due to some suspicion. Personnel from the county government and various agencies completely scattered and fled. This occurred on the 13th of this month. It is also said that the County Magistrate was newly replaced. With the old Magistrate gone, local order is also quite chaotic. The Guangdong-Fujian border benefits from convenient road transportation, with a round trip from Shantou to Zhao'an possible in one day. Deep villages in Guangdong, such as Huanggang south of Fenshuiguan and 20 li along the road on both sides of the villages, all have troops stationed. These are all situations on the Guangdong-Fujian border.

In the Changting and Liancheng areas of western Fujian, a large number of bandits and communists have recently arrived from the Jiangxi border. These bandits are also afraid of aircraft reconnaissance and often move out at dusk, returning to camp by noon the next day. As soon as they set up camp, they guard the road intersections, cutting off transportation. Each leg of the bandits' journey is 150 li, and they travel light, eating only fried rice along the way and not cooking meals. It is said that a large contingent of communist bandits has also arrived in the Yunmenling and Huichang areas. Their journeys can be calculated at 150 li per leg, suspected of coming from Shicheng and Ruijin. The bandits do not use military telephones for their movements. They establish a communication and intelligence network every five square li. In the event of military action, this network is distributed to various areas, using the method of running on foot to transmit information between A, B, C, and D. News from Liancheng can be sent to Ruijin within a few hours. It is said that the direction of the bandits is moving towards the Jiangxi-Fujian border. This intelligence network is also set up in various bandit areas and at the border between red and white areas. The garrisons in the various counties of southern Fujian are weak, and the people's self-defense capabilities are low. The prospects for public safety are extremely worrying, which is also a negative phenomenon following the Fujian Incident.

The Course of Resolving the Mongolian Autonomy Issue 102

Mongolian People's Demands Were Too High; The Central Government Set a Compromise

Principles and Organizational Laws Can Be Implemented After Approval

Chiefs of Leagues and Banners in Inner Mongolia requested the organization of an Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Deliberations began on October 9 and continued until November 11. The Minister of Internal Affairs Huang Shaojun and Vice Chairman of the Mongolian Committee Zhao Pilian went to Bailingmiao to consult with various princes several times. They combined the central government's decided plan with the Mongolian people's demands to formulate six principles. Minister Huang has now submitted these to the central government for a final decision. Based on the account of someone who participated in the meeting, the following details the before and after of this matter, the central government's original plan, the Mongolian people's initial demands, the finally drafted principles, and the organizational outline of the Mongolian League and Banner Chiefs' Autonomous Conference for the reference of those concerned about border affairs.

Meeting Process: The Inner Mongolian League and Banner Chiefs' Preparatory Conference for Autonomy held five meetings from October 9 to October 24 of this year. The first was on October 9, the second on October 15, the third on October 19, the fourth on October 22, and the fifth on the 24th of this month. As a result, 36 articles of the Organization Law of the Mongolian Autonomous Agency were passed. When Minister Huang and Vice Chairman Zhao arrived in Bailingmiao on November 11, the first three days were purely for banquets, horse racing, and chanting scriptures. From the 14th to the 17th, Minister Huang formally consulted with the Mongolian princes on the issue of Mongolian autonomy. At that time, the demands of the Mongolian people and the central government's plan differed greatly, making it impossible to reach an agreement. Therefore, on the morning of the 17th, it almost broke down. Minister Huang and others planned to return to Sui immediately. Later, through the mediation of the Panchen Lama and a group of young people, the final six principles were decided until 2 a.m. on the 18th. On the 18th, Minister Huang and others happily returned to Sui.

Central Government Plan: Plan A formulated by the central government changes the organization of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission: (1) The central government will establish a Border Affairs Department (or Mongolian and Tibetan Department) directly under the Executive Yuan as the highest central authority for handling Mongolian and Tibetan administration. It will have one Minister and two Vice Ministers to oversee the department's affairs. (2) The Border Affairs Department will establish various divisions and sections to manage affairs and various committees to be responsible for discussion and implementation. (3) The Border Affairs Department shall determine appropriate times to separately convene leaders with administrative responsibilities and individuals with virtue and prestige from various border regions to hold meetings in Beijing. (4) The Border Affairs Department shall consult with other departments and committees on matters of national administration that are mutually related and decide on how to proceed. B. A plan to reform the Mongolian local administrative system: (1) The administrative regions where provinces and counties have already been established shall not be changed. (2) Provinces with Mongolian people residing in them shall establish Mongolian Local Political Affairs Committees separately as special management agencies within those provinces to handle local administration. Each committee shall have a number of members and elect a Chairman and a Vice Chairman, all of whom shall be filled by Mongolians with virtue, prestige, political knowledge, and experience. (3) In provinces where ten local political affairs committees have already been established, except for military, diplomatic, and other national administrative matters, which shall still be handled by the central government or by the local provincial government authorized by the central government, the remaining local administration of areas where Mongolian people reside shall be the responsibility of the Mongolian Local Political Affairs Committee and shall be under the command and supervision of the Central Border Affairs Department. (4) The Mongolian Local Political Affairs Committee may, depending on the situation, divide into departments or sections to handle various administrative affairs. (5) The Mongolian Local Political Affairs Committee may, when necessary, allocate funds from the central government to subsidize various local construction projects according to the needs of each locality. (6) The Mongolian Local Political Affairs Committee may formulate local special regulations and issue orders within the scope of not violating national laws and regulations. (7) The Mongolian Local Political Affairs Committee shall also establish a Mongolian People's Representative Conference as a civil agency of the Mongolian people, which shall meet regularly once a year. The representatives shall be generated by leagues, banners, and groups as units and may use the election method. (8) The various departments and counties under the provincial government shall consult with the local political affairs committee at any time to decide on the local political affairs involving the scope of Mongolian administration, which shall be resolved by the provincial government committee or submitted to the central government for resolution. (9) The Chairman and Vice Chairman of the Mongolian Local Government Committee may attend meetings of the local provincial government committee as non-voting participants. (10) The table of Mongolian administrative system is as follows:

Departments and Committees: Various Departments

Administrative Pivot: Provincial Government

Border Affairs Department: Mongolian Local Political Affairs Committee

C. Standards for Employing Personnel in Mongolian Administration: (1) Central or local Mongolian administration should accommodate as many Mongolians as possible. (2) The central government should establish branches of the Central Military and Political School in appropriate locations, staffed by those familiar with the Mongolian situation as instructors, to cultivate Mongolian national talent in various specialties and find ways to employ them. A concrete plan to reform the Mongolian administrative system is explained in the following: According to the fourth article of the Premier's Outline of Nation-Building, the government should support the small and weak ethnic groups within the country to enable them to decide on their own affairs and achieve autonomy. The Premier solemnly declared that he recognized the right of self-determination of all ethnic groups within China. After the victory of the revolution against imperialism and warlords, a free and unified Republic of China would be organized. The Third National Congress also resolved that we must correct the evil policies of fooling Mongolia and Tibet during the Qing and warlord eras and sincerely support the economic, political, and educational development of all ethnic groups, striving to advance together towards the realm of civilization and progress. The party advocates supporting the autonomy of various ethnic groups within the country, which has long been announced to China and abroad. In order to eliminate misunderstandings among border residents and increase their interests, all Mongolian and Tibetan administrative systems, whether central or local, should be based on this spirit of self-determination and autonomy to achieve the practical results of support and development. Taking Mongolia as an example, the connection between the central organization and the Mongolian local organization in the past was loose, and the customs of the Mongolian people were different. Within the provincial region, because there was no special management agency, it was easy for misunderstandings to occur in the provincial administration, which gave those who coveted the opportunity to sow discord. On the one hand, the princes and chiefs who bear the heavy responsibility of the clan, as well as the young Mongolians who have received political training, have not been able to find political outlets, which often disappoints them. The outbreak of Inner Mongolian autonomy this time, although the cause is complex, is mainly due to the fact that the system and politics cannot fully satisfy the demands of the Mongolian people. Based on the above reasons, a concrete plan to reform the Mongolian local administrative system is proposed, and its main points are explained as follows: First, reform the Mongolian local system, with the principle of not destroying its original administrative regions and administrative system for places where provinces and counties have already been established. The establishment of provinces in the border areas is based on special regions, and the original administrative regions have long been clearly defined with the terms of a certain province and a certain county. Public and private documents have been used for a long time. The twenty-eight provinces of China are especially well-known to people in China and abroad. If they are suddenly divided, the relationship will not be superficial. Therefore, this plan advocates that the administrative regions of provinces such as Chahar and Suiyuan should not be changed due to the Mongolian people's advocacy of autonomy. As for the local administrative organization, it may be slightly supplemented to suit the actual needs. Second, although provinces have been established in places where Mongolian people gather, because of different customs, habits, languages, and religions, the past local governments have often neglected the study and reform of the Mongolian people's internal affairs, resulting in various estrangements. This is undeniable. Now, in order to remedy the defects, it is proposed to add a local political affairs committee under the provincial administrative region and the provincial administrative system, under the command and supervision of the Border Affairs Department, to specifically manage Mongolian local administration, to assist the provincial government, and to achieve the effect of separate governance. This will not only make Mongolian administration specialized, but also make the relationship between the central government and the border areas closer. Third, in order to increase the actual interests of the border people, the central government must plan and proceed with various construction projects, both material and spiritual, step by step. However, the local public and private economies are exhausted. When necessary, the Border Affairs Department should consider the needs of each locality and formulate construction plans and budgets, which should be submitted to the central government for the allocation of large amounts of money to assist, in order to appease the border people and consolidate the border defense. Fourth, various ethnic disputes occur frequently in various localities. The provincial government presides over the political affairs of the entire province and originally had a quota of Mongolian members. In the event of disputes between various departments and counties and the people, the provincial government committee can be responsible for resolving them. If necessary, the central government should be asked to handle them for the sake of convenience.

Mongolian People's Demands: Organization Law of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. The chiefs of the Inner Mongolian leagues and banners, in order to meet the actual needs of Inner Mongolia, should invoke the provisions of the Outline of Nation-Building of the National Government on self-determination and autonomy of various ethnic groups within the country, convene a plenary meeting of the chiefs of the Inner Mongolian leagues and banners, and establish the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government under the leadership of the National Government, and formulate the Organization Law of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government, which is promulgated as follows: Chapter I, Autonomous Government. Article 1, The Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall have overall control over the autonomous powers of the Inner Mongolian leagues and banners. Article 2, The Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall take the original territories of the Inner Mongolian leagues and banners as its jurisdictional scope. Article 3, Except for international military and diplomatic matters, which shall be handled by the central government, all administrative affairs of Inner Mongolia shall be carried out in accordance with the laws and orders of this Autonomous Government. Article 4, The Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall be organized by the Political Affairs Hall, the Legal Affairs Committee, and the Council Hall. However, when the facts require it, the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government and its various halls and committees may establish special agencies as appropriate. Article 5, The Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall have one Chairman, two Vice Chairmen, and nine to fifteen members. Article 6, The Chairman and Vice Chairmen of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall be jointly elected by the chiefs of the leagues and banners. The heads of the halls and the chairmen of the committees shall be concurrently held by government members. The deputy heads of the halls and the vice chairmen of the committees shall be nominated by the heads of the halls and the chairmen of the committees and appointed by the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Article 7, When the Chairman of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government is unable to perform his duties due to an accident, he shall be represented by the Vice Chairman or the Head of the Political Affairs Hall. Article 8, The Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall form a government committee with the members of the government. The Chairman shall be the Chairman of the government committee. Article 9, The Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall promulgate laws and issue orders after the resolution of the government committee meeting, and the Chairman and Vice Chairman of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall temporarily sign the name of the head of the competent authority in charge of the relationship to implement it. Article 10, Matters that cannot be resolved between the various halls and committees of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall be resolved by the government committee meeting. Article 11, The various halls and committees of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government may issue hall orders and committee orders within the scope of not conflicting with the laws and regulations of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Article 12, The Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government shall establish the following two offices: (1) Secretariat, (2) General Affairs Office. Article 13, The Secretariat shall be responsible for the following matters: (1) Matters concerning the receipt, dispatch, compilation, and custody of documents. (2) Matters concerning the distribution of documents. (3) Matters concerning the drafting and translation of documents. (4) Matters concerning the custody of seals. (5) Matters concerning the compilation of government gazettes and agendas and meeting minutes, etc. (6) Matters concerning the registration of the appointment and removal of officials in the government. (7) Matters concerning the issuance of orders. Article 14, The General Affairs Office shall be responsible for the following matters: (1) Matters concerning the compilation of statistics and reports. (2) Matters concerning accounting and general affairs. (3) Matters not belonging to the Secretariat. Chapter II, Political Affairs Hall. Article 15, The Political Affairs Hall shall be the highest administrative organ of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Article 16, The Political Affairs Hall shall have one head and two deputy heads. When the head of the hall is unable to perform his duties due to an accident, he shall be represented by the deputy head. Article 17, The Political Affairs Hall shall establish the following departments to share the power of administration: (1) Internal Affairs Department, (2) Garrison Department, (3) Finance Department, (4) Education Department, (5) Justice Department, (6) Construction Department, (7) Industry Department, (8) Public Relations Department. Article 18, The head and deputy heads of the Political Affairs Hall and the heads and deputy heads of each department and the heads of special agencies shall organize a hall affairs meeting to handle all administrative affairs. The head of the hall shall be the chairman of the meeting. Article 19, The Political Affairs Hall may add or merge departments and other agencies with the resolution of the government committee meeting and the Legal Affairs Committee. Article 20, Matters that cannot be resolved between the various departments and special agencies of the Political Affairs Hall shall be resolved by the hall affairs meeting. Article 21, Each department of the Political Affairs Hall shall have one head and one deputy head, all of whom shall be nominated by the head of the Political Affairs Hall and appointed by the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Article 22, The head and deputy heads of the Political Affairs Hall and the heads of each department may attend the government committee meeting and the Legal Affairs Committee meeting when necessary. Article 23, The Political Affairs Hall may submit proposals to the Legal Affairs Committee on matters under its jurisdiction. Article 24, The organizational law of the Political Affairs Hall and each department shall be stipulated by law by the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Chapter III, Legal Affairs Committee. Article 25, The Legal Affairs Committee shall be the highest legislative organ of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Article 26, The Legal Affairs Committee shall have one chairman, two vice chairmen, and seventeen to twenty-nine members. When the chairman is unable to perform his duties due to an accident, he shall be represented by the vice chairman. Article 27, The members of the Legal Affairs Committee shall be nominated by the chairman and appointed by the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Article 28, The chairman of the Legal Affairs Committee shall be the chairman of the meeting. Article 29, The resolutions of the Legal Affairs Committee shall be promulgated after being resolved by the government committee meeting. Article 30, The organizational law of the Legal Affairs Committee shall be stipulated by law by the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Chapter IV, Council Hall. Article 31, The Council Hall shall be the highest advisory and recommending organ of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Article 32, The Council Hall shall have one head, two deputy heads, and twenty-one to forty-one councilors. The councilors shall be nominated by the head of the hall and appointed by the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. When the head of the hall is unable to perform his duties due to an accident, he shall be represented by the deputy head. Article 33, The councilors of the Council Hall shall organize a council, and its powers shall be as follows: (1) Matters concerning the advisory of the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. (2) Matters specially handled by the Chairman of the Government Committee. (3) Matters concerning the review of proposals recommended by the councilors. (4) Other important matters. Article 34, The head of the Council Hall shall be the chairman of the council. Article 35, The organizational law of the Council Hall shall be stipulated by law by the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Government. Chapter V, Supplementary Provisions. Article 36, This organizational law shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Through Ups and Downs: After the five princes proposed the organizational methods of the autonomous government, Minister Huang believed that their demands were too extravagant and seemed to have a tendency to break away from the central government. After repeatedly explaining the central government's intentions and the central government's original plan, the chiefs of the leagues and banners gathered to discuss the central government's plan in detail and agreed on eleven articles, expressing a step back. However, Minister Huang still believed that it was not in line with the central government's intention to guide Mongolian autonomy, and he further instructed them on the close relationship between Han and Mongolian, and the interests and harms involved. The princes then discussed again and decided on six principles.

Final Principles: The six principles finally decided on the issue of Inner Mongolian autonomy: (1) Name: It shall be named the First Autonomous Region Government of Mongolia, the Second Autonomous Region Government of Mongolia, and so on. (2) Region: The Silingol League and the Chahar Banner shall be compiled into the First Autonomous Region of Mongolia, and the Yiwu and Yi leagues and the Tumote Alashan and Ejina leagues shall be compiled into the Second Autonomous Region of Mongolia. Other leagues and banners shall be compiled according to the ratio. (3) Subordination: The Mongolian autonomous region governments shall be directly under the Executive Yuan. In the event of incidents involving provinces, they shall be handled in consultation with the provincial government. (4) Powers: The Mongolian autonomous region governments shall manage all political affairs of the leagues and banners within their respective regions. (5) Funding: The expenses of the Mongolian autonomous governments shall be allocated by the central government on a monthly basis. (6) Liaison: A joint conference shall be established between the Mongolian autonomous halls, organized by one representative from each banner in each autonomous region, to discuss and decide on common matters between the autonomous regions.

Autonomous Conference: The organizational outline of the Inner Mongolian League and Banner Chiefs' Autonomous Conference. Article 1, In order to realize Inner Mongolian autonomy, the Inner Mongolian League and Banner Chiefs shall convene an Inner Mongolian Autonomous Conference in Bailingmiao. Article 2, Attendees of this conference shall be the chiefs of the leagues and banners or other representatives. Representatives of Mongolian groups and secretaries of the chiefs may attend. Article 3, This conference shall mutually elect five people to form a presidium to preside over all affairs of this conference. Article 4, This conference shall establish a secretariat to handle affairs separately in various groups: Document Group, Deliberation Group, Propaganda Group, Translation Group, Finance Group, General Affairs Group, Public Relations Group, and Security Group. Article 5, The secretariat shall have one secretary general, who shall, under the orders of the presidium, manage the affairs of the secretariat. Each group shall have one director, who shall, under the orders of the secretary general, preside over the affairs of each group. The secretariat shall have a number of secretaries, clerks, and scribes to handle affairs in each group. Article 6, The rules of procedure and rules of business of this conference shall be determined separately. Article 7, This conference shall end when the Inner Mongolian Autonomous Conference is realized. Article 8, This outline shall be implemented from the date of its adoption by the conference.

Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway and Zhejiang Province's Future Prosperity Plan 103

Connecting Eastern Zhejiang, and Reaching Jinhua, Quzhou, Yan Prefecture, Ningbo, Shaoxing, Taizhou, Wenzhou, and Chu Prefecture

Many Scenic Spots Along Each Prefecture, Future Tourists Will Surely Be Numerous

The Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway has been fully completed and is scheduled to open on the 28th. Afterwards, not only will Zhejiang Province be connected, and culture and economy develop evenly, but the province's prosperity plan will also be gradually realized.

According to the planned Hangzhou-Jiangshan route, it was originally a section of the Southeast Railway system personally designated by Sun Yat-sen. In the future, with extensions, one end can pass through the Eastern Great Port, and the other end can extend to Nanchang, connecting to the Nanxun Railway, and then to Pingxiang, connecting with the Yuehan Railway, and can directly reach Guangzhou. It is heard that the authorities' plan to prosper Zhejiang Province takes Hangzhou as the hub for commodity exports, and Zhapu, the Eastern Great Port, as the main center for attracting foreign investment. Therefore, the construction of highways is based on this principle. Many highways in the upper reaches of the Qiantang River are connected to the stations along the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway. Moreover, due to the completion of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway, transportation is convenient to the famous scenic spots in various places of the Upper Yangtze, and the number of tourists will increase. The benefit to future prosperity is as expected. The reporter will now describe the authorities' prosperity plan and the relationship between the completion of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway and prosperity, in the following, which should be welcome news to those who care about the construction of Zhejiang Province.

The Plan to Prosper the Whole Province: Creating an Oriental Switzerland. The Provincial Highway Bureau believes that Zhejiang Province has many scenic spots. If transportation can be improved and tourists attracted, the number of visitors will increase, and revenue will increase daily. This will directly benefit people's livelihoods and indirectly regulate finance. Therefore, a plan was drafted and submitted to the department for review. The preliminary plan is: (1) To construct branch roads, rest pavilions, etc., in the scenic spots and historical sites near the completed highways within the possible scope. (2) To preserve historical sites. (3) To set up telephones, bathhouses, sports fields, and gasoline emergency relief stations in various scenic areas. The second step of the plan is to establish a tourist visiting agency, divided into six sections. Those who can fluently speak several foreign languages ​​will be assigned to the guiding section. Those who are familiar with the characteristics of various scenic spots and have thoroughly studied the province's history will be assigned to the publicity section. The trust, security, relief, and general road sections are all related to the safety and convenience of travelers. If it can be implemented according to the plan, Zhejiang Province becoming an Oriental Switzerland is as expected. The construction of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway is actually the hub for the connection of various highways.

Completion of Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway Connects Transportation in Eastern Zhejiang. Now that the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway has been completed, the Construction Department is proceeding with the construction of the Xingqun Qiantang River Iron Bridge, and has agreed with the Ministry of Railways to connect the Hangzhou-Ningbo section of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway. In the future, Hangzhou can directly reach Ningbo and transfer to the Yin-Feng Highway, Yin-Zhen-Ci Road, Fengxin Road, Xin-Tian-Lin Road (Xinchang from Tiantai to Lin'an), and the stations along the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway are mostly connected to various highways, such as Hangzhou-Shaoxing Road (Hangzhou to Shaoxing), Pu-Zhong Road (Pujiang to Zhengjiachang), Yi-Chang Road (Yiwu via Dongyang to Changle Town, Sheng County), Jin-Yong-Wu Road (Jinhua to Yongkang and Wuyi), Yong-Jin Road (Yongkang to Jinyun), Jin-Man Road (Jinyun to Suichang), Li-Qing Road (Lishui to Qingtian), Qing-Wen Road (Qingtian to Yongjia), Yong-Rui-Ping Road (Yongjia via Rui'an to the Fujian border), Long-Sui-Chang Road (Longyou via Suichang to Songyang), Lan-Shou Road (Lanxi to Shouchang), Tun-Jian-Shou Road (Jiande to the Anhui border and Luotongbu to Shouchang), Chun-Sui Road (Chunan to Suian), Jiang-Chang-Kai Road (Jiangshan, Changshan, Kaihua), Sui-Kai Road (Suian to Kaihua), Qu-Guang Road (Quzhou to Guangfeng), etc., are all interconnected. Therefore, although the route only passes through the counties of Shaoxing, Jinhua, and Quzhou old prefectures, it actually connects the old prefectures of Eastern Zhejiang, Jinhua, Quzhou, Yan Prefecture, Ningbo, Shaoxing, Taizhou, Wenzhou, and Chu Prefecture, all interconnected and accessible. The completion of this road and its relation to the future prosperity of Zhejiang Province can be seen from this. Hangzhou's transportation in western Zhejiang is known to be developed, including the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway, the Hangzhou-Hui Highway, the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway, the Hangzhou-Fuyang Road (Hangzhou to Fuyang), the Fu-Xin Road (Fuyang to Tonglu), the Tong-Jian Road (Tonglu to Jiande). The Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway has a branch road to Mogan Mountain, and the Hangzhou-Hui Highway passes through Tianmu Mountain in Yuqian, both of which are scenic areas. Zhapu is the location of the Eastern Great Port personally designated by Sun Yat-sen. Since the construction of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway, foreigners flock there during the summer to swim and escape the heat, and land prices have soared. If it can be actively promoted, Zhapu will become a prosperous area.

Mountains Meander into Zhejiang, Many Scenic Spots Along the Route. Zhejiang Province's mountains belong to the Nanling Mountain system. The Xianxia Ridge stretches along the Zhejiang-Fujian border, and the Huaiyu Mountain stands on the Zhejiang-Jiangxi border. From here, it meanders into Zhejiang, forming the Kuocang, Dapen, Tiantai, Kuaiji, and Fengling mountain ranges. Therefore, the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Road east of Zhuji has undulating hills and forms strange peaks and beautiful scenery. The scenic spots near the stations along the route are the Tingxiang Lake, Yue Wang City, Yijian Pavilion, and Xiandang Mountain at Xiaoshan Station; the Zilu Village, Jia Cliff, and Wuxie at Zhuji Station; Shengyan, Zhugongyan, and Baiyun Cave at Yiwu; the North Mountain and Fangyan at Jinhua Station; the Fuzhen Temple and Dongfeng Pavilion at Lanxi Station; the Jiufeng Mountain at Dongyuan Tangxi Station; the Sandie Mountain at Huzhen Station; Xiaonanmei (also known as Tongdadian) and Zhaoqing Temple at Longyuan Station; Longshan Temple at Hecun Station; Sanpian Stone at Jiangshan Station; Huaiyu Mountain at Yushan Station; Wuan Mountain Heling Temple. Among them, the most praised by tourists are Wuxie North Mountain, Fangyan, and Xianxia Ridge. The height of the Donglongtan waterfall in Wuxie is equal to the height of the hidden pool in Xuesai. The North Mountain has Chaozhen Water Jug, Shuanglong and other caves. Fangyan is in Yongkang, 200 zhang high, and the Hugong Temple is located there. The surrounding mountains have many caves of different sizes. Xianxia Ridge is eighty or ninety li away from Jiangshan, and can be reached by car. It is known for its majestic grandeur.

Songjiang

Announcement of the Re-election of the County Chamber of Commerce 104

The term of office for the incumbent committee members of the County Chamber of Commerce has expired. According to the regulations, seven of the fifteen executive committee members and three of the seven supervisory committee members should be removed, and a full number of replacements should be re-elected. Today (25th) at 9:00 AM, County Commissioner Xu Mojia and Party Commissioner Sun Shiheng attended the members' meeting. In addition to discussing routine matters, a temporary motion was proposed to request the central government to send troops to suppress the Min bandits, which was unanimously passed. After the discussion, County Commissioner Xu Mojia publicly conducted the drawing of lots. The seven executive committee members drawn were Zhang Jiliang, Wu Zhengping, Zhang Qingquan, Li Xiaojin, Zhang Mengxing, Zhang Hanshi, and Wang Zuoting. The three supervisory committee members drawn were Hong Songqiao, Xu Yajie, and Wang Songxian. In the afternoon, an election was held with 317 registered members and 309 voters. The election filled the vacancies for the seven removed executive committee members and the three supervisory committee members. The elected executive committee members were Shu Baoshan, Xu Yajie, Lu Shuchen, Liu Gulu, Gan Weiru, Wu Bisong, and Song Lianjiang. The elected supervisory committee members were Zhang Mengxing, Zhang Jiliang, and Zhang Liren.

Suzhou

Ningbo Teenager Commits Suicide in Suzhou 105

A Ningbo teenager, surnamed Dai, aged 25, arrived in Suzhou from Jiaxing on the 23rd and stayed at No. 75 Dongwu Hotel. On the 24th, he took a carriage to Tiger Hill for sightseeing and returned. Suddenly, he secretly took Lysol solution to commit suicide. He was sent to Su Yong Hospital, but his breath was faint. According to the doctor, there was little hope of saving his life. He left a distorted poem with a slight hint of pessimism. However, the cause and origin were not mentioned. On the Dongwu Hotel guest book, only the surname Dai was registered without a first name. Therefore, it is difficult to find his family.

Wuxi

Fang Juehui Visits Wuxi for Sightseeing 106

Central Committee member Fang Juehui (Yu Qiao), who was recently dispatched by Chiang Kai-shek to Jinan to meet with Han Fuju to discuss important public affairs, returned to Nanjing. Admiring the scenery of Lake Jing in our county, he made a special trip the day before yesterday, accompanied by his secretary, to visit Bai Heng and the tenth army councilor Liang Tian, ​​taking the Shanghai-Nanjing express train and arriving at 1:28 PM. After getting off the train, he took a car to Huishan to visit the famous Second Spring, and then to Meiwu, staying at the Taihu Hotel. Yesterday, Central Committee members Miao Bin, He Ziwu, and local residents Zhu Shikang, Yang Hanxi, as well as County Magistrate Yan and Police Chief Li, accompanied him to visit Taihu Lake, Huizhu, Xiaojishan and other scenic spots. Afterwards, Fang had a vegetarian meal at Guangfu Temple and did not return to the hotel until dusk. He is scheduled to leave Wuxi for Shanghai today.

Wage Disputes After the Closure of Two Silk Factories 107

Due to the extreme decline of the silk market, various silk factories in Wuxi have successively closed down. Workers have repeatedly filed disputes over wages, which are heard almost daily. The turbulent situations of the Taixin and Qingfeng factories are recorded below. (1) Qingfeng Silk Factory outside the South Gate of Jiacheng owed more than 7,000 yuan in wages after its closure. The factory owner and manager, Mr. Yao Juncheng, hid in Shanghai. Factory employees Shen Guoying, Yan Zichen, and Hui Jizhi went to Shanghai to search for him. Unexpectedly, Yao had abandoned his luggage and fled. Shen and others had no choice but to return to Wuxi. Because Yao was a wealthy merchant in Changzhou, with enough property to cover the factory's owed wages, they specially sent a letter to the Wujin Chamber of Commerce yesterday, urging Yao to come to Wuxi to handle the matter. (2) Taixin Silk Factory in Zhoushanbang ceased operations after the warehouse was burned down on the 24th of last month, using this as an excuse. The staff in the factory lived by mortgaging their belongings. Now there is nothing left to pawn. The wages owed have also been defaulted repeatedly. Manager Xu Junjie is hiding near Yong'an Bridge. Yesterday, more than 40 male and female workers went to surround him, demanding wages. Xu had no way to respond, so he jumped over the wall and fled. The workers waited for a long time in vain, so they obtained several dou of white rice from his family to satisfy their hunger. They will continue to sit and demand payment in the future.

Zhenjiang

County Magistrate of Chongming Accused 108

Shen Jiang, the county magistrate of Chongming, has been transferred from Dongtai County to Chongming for more than two years. He has been indifferent to local affairs, and local people have long been dissatisfied. Recently, due to ineffective disaster relief and the withholding of 5,000 yuan allocated by the province for disaster relief for twenty years, as well as the red pill manufacturing case in Xixiang, the situation has become even more uproar. Local residents Wang Zenglu, Qu Jiyang, Cheng Qixia, and Huang Jinping separately filed accusations with the province. The disaster victims also reported to the Jiangsu, Chuan, Nan, Chong, Bao, and Qi Five-County Flood Relief Association that County Magistrate Shen was ineffective in disaster relief. The Shanghai gentry Lu Caifu and Wang Qingmu also filed an impeachment with the Flood Relief Association, which has already forwarded it to the provincial government for investigation and punishment. The day before yesterday, Wang Qingmu submitted a separate petition to the province, accusing County Magistrate Shen of withholding disaster relief funds and requesting his removal.

Danyang

Robbery Cases in Southeast Villages 110

Zhang Weizhou's house, a rich farmer in Xidabo Village, Dongxiang, was suddenly visited by more than 20 bandits at about 11 o'clock the night before last. Each held guns and weapons, climbed over the wall and entered, searching and looting wildly. Not yet satisfied, they injured the face of the owner's wife, Zhao, and forced her to hand over silver dollars before leaving with a hoot. Zhou Mingfu's house in Xiaqin Village was also visited by more than 10 bandits at about 1 o'clock the night before last. They jumped over the wall and entered, overturning boxes and chests and searching everywhere. They tied up the owner and extorted money. Fortunately, the family members were alert and went out to beat the gong and call for help. The bandits fled with the loot.

Jiaxing

Explosion While Making Sulfur Blocks Injures People 111

Zhang Wenhua, a carpenter living at No. 26 Xiaolu North, Xiatang Street, Jiaxing, is 32 years old. Now that he is unemployed and has no way to make a living, he came up with a fantastic idea to use sulfur and other materials, mixed with bowl shards, lard, and fish meat, to make granules. He would throw them on the ground in the countryside so that wild cats and other animals would eat them and be blown to death, and then he would skin them and sell the skins for money. At noon on the 24th, Zhang was again preparing in the house as usual. Due to careless smoking, the sulfur caught fire and exploded, making a loud noise and causing smoke and mist to fill the air. Nearby residents were quite frightened. Zhang Mingsu, who lived with him, was injured in the explosion. The first police station arrested Zhang and sent him to the Public Security Bureau on charges of endangering public safety. On the 25th, he was transferred to the court for interrogation.

Hangzhou

Falsely Accused Thief Commits Suicide in Anger 112

Qian Kejia, a service worker at the Hangzhou Huaguang Lane Telephone Branch, was falsely accused of being a thief by a clerk named Meng. In anger, he drank Lysol in an attempt to commit suicide. However, he was unable to die immediately, so he used a knife to cut his throat, breaking his esophagus and causing blood to flow like a gush. He fainted immediately. Fortunately, he was discovered and rushed to the Municipal Hospital for treatment, but his injuries were so severe that his life was feared.

Worker at Sanyou Factory Crushed to Death by Machine Wheel 113

Xie Donglin, a worker at the Hangzhou factory of Sanyou Industrial Company in Gongchenqiao, Hangzhou, had worked in the factory for many years. He had a mother, wife, and many children at home. Unexpectedly, Xie was working on the motor at about 10 o'clock yesterday morning when he was accidentally caught in the belt, crushing his hand. He immediately lost consciousness and blood flowed all over the ground. His colleagues reported to the factory owner and sent him to Guangji Hospital in the city for treatment. By the time he arrived at the hospital gate, he had already stopped breathing.

Central Committee members Zhang Ji, Ma Chaojun, Wang Luyi, Chen Zhaoying, and others, who were dispatched by the Central Government to the Southwest to exchange views on the current situation and discuss various issues of national salvation, returned to Shanghai on the Jefferson President Wheel from Hong Kong at 8:30 yesterday morning. Mayor Wu Tiecheng of this city hosted a banquet at the Foreign Guests Reception Center on Xialong Road at noon yesterday to welcome Zhang and other four committee members, who ran for peace this time and worked for the country. We are sincerely concerned that the current situation is serious, and we should shoulder the heavy responsibility of the country. We are concerned that there is no way to stabilize internal and external conflicts, and to resist external aggression, in order to live up to the expectations of the people. This matter has also been discussed with comrades in the south. Furthermore, the Fourth Plenary Session will be held. In order to rectify and clarify party affairs and politics, the Central Government eagerly expects comrades in the south to express their opinions. We first went to Hong Kong to meet with Committee Member Hu Hanmin, and then went to Guangzhou to visit the Executive Department members Xiao Focheng, Deng Zeru, Chen Jitang, Zou Lu, Lin Yunga, Lin Yizhong, Liu Jiwen, Qu Fangpu, Huang Jilu, and other committee members and comrades, and conveyed the central government's intentions one by one. Then, from Guangzhou, we went to Nanning to meet with Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, Huang Xuchu, and other Central Committee members in Guangxi. After returning to Guangdong, we met with Tang Shaochuan again. We went to Hong Kong again to visit Committee Member Hu Hanmin and Committee Member Wu Chaoshu. The situation of the talks everywhere was very cordial and harmonious. This Fourth Plenary Session will definitely have precise and practical plans that will be jointly proposed for discussion, in order to break the current crisis faced by the country and the nation, and to develop a new life in party affairs and politics. As for the Fujian Incident, comrades in Hong Kong, Shanghai, and the two Guangdongs unanimously believe that it is absurd and incomparable and must be strictly corrected. Otherwise, the life of the country and the nation will be cut off and exhausted by the rebels. We will now turn to Nanjing to report our mandate. At this point in national affairs, the people's expectations of those who shoulder the burden of the party and government are extremely strict and urgent. It is our hope that we can work together to achieve success and discuss a path to revival together.

Zhang Ji Meets Reporters. After the three Central Committee members, Zhang and others, arrived at the East Asia Hotel, reporters from various newspapers visited one after another, and Zhang met with them one after another, talking eloquently, without any tiredness. Zhang first described the journey, saying that when we first arrived in Hong Kong by boat, we met with Mr. Hu Zhantang twice, and when we returned via Wusong, we met with Mr. Hu again. In Guangdong, we had in-depth conversations with Xiao Focheng, Deng Zeru, Chen Jitang, Tang Shaoyi, Zou Lu, and other members. Severe Sanctions Against Fujian. The Southwest believes that Chen Mingshu and others are absurd and do not approve of the Fujian rebellion. The method of dealing with the Fujian rebellion should be to impose sanctions. However, the opinions of each person on the method of sanctions were not consistent. If there is no unity, nothing can be accomplished. Even Li Zongren said in his telegram to us that at this point in national affairs, unity is essential.

Grand Cleaning Campaign Kicks Off Yesterday 120

Entire Corps of Sanitation Workers Deployed in the Morning

Motorcade Parade Through North and South Shanghai in the Afternoon

The Municipal Health Bureau, in conjunction with the Public Safety Bureau, launched the tenth annual grand cleaning campaign yesterday. Over three hundred sanitation workers were organized and paraded through the north and south of the city. Public cleanliness slogans were posted all over the streets and alleys. The Municipal Public Safety Bureau also piloted a new garbage disposal method in the jurisdiction of the Second Precinct of the Second District. Details of the situation are recorded below:

Morning Operations　The city-wide cleanliness campaign commenced at 9:00 AM yesterday. The Cleansing Division of the Second Department of the Health Bureau dispatched twenty inspectors to supervise the entire corps of over three hundred sanitation workers. Equipped with cleaning tools, they worked in groups alongside police officers from the various district precincts of the Municipal Public Safety Bureau. While the sanitation workers swept the streets, the inspectors and police officers distributed flyers and slogans door-to-door, advising residents and businesses along the streets to pay attention to both domestic and public hygiene. The efforts were quite thorough.

Afternoon Parade　At 1:00 PM, a cleanliness parade was held in the north and south of the city. The Municipal Health Bureau hired twelve trucks and over thirty bicycles. The Municipal Public Safety Bureau dispatched fifteen motorcycles. The parade assembled in front of the Health Bureau in Maojia Lane, outside the South City. The head of the Cleansing Division, Director Jiang, a technician from the Central Health Administration, and the inspectors led the entire corps of sanitation workers to set off. The trucks were decorated with bamboo-framed cloth banners. The sanitation workers carried brooms and iron shovels on their shoulders, wore yellow vests trimmed with red, with the characters "Qing Dao" [Cleaning Road] embedded in the middle, and carried flags. They shouted slogans along the way. Inspectors distributed flyers on either side of the trucks to attract public attention. The parade concluded in the north and south of the city at 4:20 PM.

Route　(1) The route for the parade in Southern Shanghai began at Maojia Lane, passed through Wai Ma Lu, Zhonghua Road, Qijia Road, exited the Great East Gate, passed through Minguo Road, Fangbang Road, exited the Small East Gate, circled inside Ma Lu, and returned to Maojia Lane to disperse. (2) The route for the parade in Zhabei started at Minli Road, passed through Gonghe Road, Gonghe Xin Yao, Qiujiang Road, Guangdong Street, Baoyuan Road, Baoxing Road, Baoshan Road, Xinmin Road, Datong Road, Guangfu Road, and Hengfeng Road, circled back to Gonghe Road, Minli Road, and dispersed.

Yesterday's Yunnan Uprising Commemoration 121

Municipal Party Headquarters Convened a General Assembly Yesterday

Li Liejun Hosted a Banquet for Old Comrades

Municipal Party Headquarters　Yesterday marked the eighteenth anniversary of the Yunnan Uprising. A commemorative meeting was held at 10:00 AM, convening representatives from all walks of life. Attendees included Wang Zongjian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs.

Cleanliness Slogans　The Municipal Health Bureau posted slogans for the twelfth cleanliness campaign in various streets and alleys, including "Maintain Street Cleanliness," "To Maintain Health, Pay Attention to Cleanliness," "Do Not Dump Garbage Anywhere," "Do Not Spit Anywhere," "Do Not Urinate or Defecate Anywhere," "Pay Attention to Public Hygiene," "Damaging the Streets Hinders the City's Cleanliness," "To Keep the Streets Clean, First, Refrain from Damaging Them," and over ten other common slogans with easily understood meanings.

Garbage Disposal　The Health and Public Safety Bureaus jointly posted a notice the day before yesterday to pilot a new garbage disposal method in the Second Precinct of the Second District. If successful, it will be gradually implemented citywide. Yesterday, the precinct dispatched patrol officers and two police officers to investigate door-to-door, removing old wooden and cement garbage bins at the entrances of the lanes. Eighty to ninety percent of shops and residents in the area had prepared new-style garbage bins. Those who had not were immediately urged to build them. Starting this morning, from 8:00 AM to 11:00 AM and from 2:00 PM to 5:00 PM, sanitation workers from the Health Bureau will ring bells to notify the shops to dispose of their garbage.

Chamber of Commerce Notification　The Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to notify all shops and factories to carry out a major cleaning and assist in the sanitation campaign. The original recorded text is as follows: "Approved Health Bureau official letter No. 5904 states, 'The twelfth sanitation campaign in this city has been scheduled for the 25th of this month. Special attention will be paid to uniting citizens to carry out the cleaning of dirt and grime. Therefore, please inform the various industrial and commercial groups to notify all factories and shops to carry out a major cleaning and wash all walls, doors, and windows clean, arousing a sense of cleanliness and beauty in everyone to promote this. According to our country's old customs, each household originally had the act of sweeping the eaves, but most were unable to effectively implement it. This major cleaning is originally intended to awaken implementation. Please inform all factories and shops to earnestly implement it.' and so on. Approved, it is hereby ordered that the Chamber of Commerce be notified and instruct all trade associations to comply. This order." It is heard that the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has already forwarded letters to the various trade associations in the city, instructing members to implement it.

Qiu Yunming of the Land Bureau, Zhang Yichen of the National Association for the Study of Confucian Teachings, Huang Zaoxiong of the Municipal Education Association, Wang Shunfa of the Second Special District Citizens' Federation, Mao Yun, He Yuanming of the Accountants' Association, Zhou Xuexiang of the General Labor Union, and over two hundred representatives from various labor unions, schools, and levels of party headquarters, chaired by Tong Xingbai, recorded by Zhu Xiaochun, and emceed by Zhang Hanyun, performed the rituals as usual. The chairman then reported on the Yunnan Uprising, stating (1) that we should follow the Premier's call to instill genuine democratic ideas into the masses and establish a genuine democratic nation. To achieve this goal, we must go through the period of political tutelage to avoid repeating the mistakes of the Xinhai Revolution. (2) The purpose of the Yunnan Uprising was to support the Republic of China and overthrow the imperial system. Recently, Chen Mingshu, Li Jishen, etc., under the guise of public opinion, changed the era name and established a system, which is the same as Yuan Shikai's self-amusement of proclaiming himself emperor. Both are acts that endanger the Republic of China. It is hoped that the people of the whole country will unanimously condemn them to establish a democratic nation and be worthy of the martyrs of the Yunnan Uprising. The meeting ended with slogans.

Li Liejun　Seventeen years ago, during the Yunnan Uprising, Li Liejun, along with Cai Songpo, Tang Jiyao, Luo Rongxuan, etc., led the troops to fight against Yuan Shikai and save the Republic of China from crisis. His contribution was great. Yesterday, on the anniversary of the Yunnan Uprising, Li Liejun, remembering his comrades who had risen up together in the past, now few and far between, and the deaths of Cai Geng and others, was deeply moved by the past and the present. Therefore, he specially gathered his old friends and colleagues at his residence on Rue Massenet yesterday at noon for a luncheon. Among those present were Xu Yuangao, former Secretary-General of the Second Army of the National Protection Army, Zhong Dong, Chief Counselor, Jin Weiqian, Chief of Staff, and Chen Rongsheng, and over twenty others. At the beginning of the meal, everyone observed five minutes of silence in memory of the martyrs. Then, they drank heartily and talked about the vicissitudes of life. After the meal, they showed each other correspondence and memorabilia, reminisced for a long time, and sighed endlessly. In the past two days, Li Liejun had received dozens of letters and telegrams of condolences from various parties, praising Li Liejun's efforts to overthrow Hongxian's imperial system and rebuild the Republic of China, wishing Li Liejun well for the country. Li Liejun was extremely grateful for the kindness of all parties and ordered his secretary Zhang Mi Gong to reply to each and express his gratitude. Li Liejun also spoke to reporters from various newspapers yesterday, saying that today is the anniversary of the Yunnan National Protection War against Yuan. Looking back on the past, it has been seventeen years. At that time, in the early days of the revolution and nation-building, everyone had great enthusiasm for implementing democracy and revitalizing China. Military and civilian leaders in various provinces were also able to solemnly protect their personal concepts and did not willingly submit to the powerful and become vassals. They sought only freedom and equality for the people of the whole country, without any discrimination. Therefore, when we called for justice, the response was overwhelming. Although we raised troops in remote areas, we were able to strip Yuan Shikai of his courage and ensure the safety of the republican system. This was not something that mere strong soldiers and brave generals could achieve, but was due to the support of the people. If the party members of today could still maintain the spirit of nation-building in the past, and enable the party to return to unity, and the people of the country to fully realize their intelligence, then the ruined national affairs can still be saved. I am old and unable to help with the difficulties of the times, and I am ashamed to face Cai Songpo, Tang Diying, Liu Ruzhou, and Luo Rongxuan underground.
